# Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs

Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.

Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.

<HARD-GATE>
Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
</HARD-GATE>

## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"

Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.

## Checklist

You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:

1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
9. **Transition to implementation**

I found several relevant resources about converting OpenStreetMap data to 3D worlds with three.js and other 3D engines. Here's what the search revealed:

## Key Approaches

**OpenStreetMap Data Format**: GeoJSON files contain various elements of the map like roads, parks, buildings represented by an array of various coordinates and metadata.

**Data Extraction**: Using the OverPass API took time, as the documentation doesn't make it clear how to structure its query language. The OverPass API allows querying for specific map features like buildings, highways, water features, and parks.

**Three.js Implementation**: The solution was to merge all the buildings into one big mesh, instead of spawning individual objects for each building. This approach causes a side effect that all buildings will have the same material, but it was worth it due to the massively improved performance.

**Performance Considerations

Several games have been built using OpenStreetMap data, enabling the creation of games set in the real world.

**Notable Games:**

1. **Dozor: Moscow** - An online multiplayer RPG set in modern Moscow, offering city exploration, quests, real-time battles, and the eternal struggle between Light and Darkness.

3. **Open Path** - An open source, browser-based, online RPG that aims to be the best game engine available, boasting many inbuilt features that most frameworks don't have.

4. **Infection Free Zone** - A survival/city builder game where you choose a place in the world to defend from zombies using footprints and semantic tags from OSM.

### 🤖 Assistant  ·  _2026-07-17T08:05:38.004Z_

Babylon.js + Huế it is — great location for this: the Citadel, Perfume River, Trang Tien Bridge, and Thien Mu Pagoda make a naturally quest-able map. Here's the design, section by section.

## Design: "Huế Quest" (working title)

### 1. Concept
Single-player browser game. You wander a stylized low-poly Huế — real street/river/landmark layout from OpenStreetMap, hand-decorated — in third-person view with a follow camera. You talk to NPCs and complete 1–2 short quests that route you between real landmarks (e.g., Dong Ba Market → Trang Tien Bridge → the Citadel gate → Thien Mu Pagoda). Demo scope: one district (~1.5 × 1.5 km around the Perfume River), ~5 NPCs, 2 quests, one playable session of ~5 minutes.

### 2. Stack
- **Babylon.js (latest) + Vite + TypeScript**, no framework for UI.
- **Collision, not physics:** Babylon's built-in `moveWithCollisions` + gravity instead of a full physics engine (Havok). A walking-and-talking game doesn't need rigid-body physics, and skipping it removes a whole class of hackathon bugs.
- **Character:** free rigged low-poly GLB (Quaternius/Mixamo) with idle/walk/run animations.
- **UI (dialogue, quest log, hints):** plain HTML/CSS overlay on top of the canvas — simpler and faster to style than Babylon GUI.

### 3. World pipeline (the "hybrid" part)
Two stages, so the game never depends on live map APIs:

1. **Build-time script** (Node, run once): queries the Overpass API for a bounding box around central Huế — building footprints, roads, the river, the Citadel walls/moat — converts lat/lon to local meters, simplifies geometry, and writes a `world.json` checked into the repo.
2. **Runtime:** Babylon reads `world.json` and builds the world: flat ground, extruded buildings merged into one mesh (flat pastel low-poly palette), roads as ribbons, a water plane for the river, the moat around the Citadel.
3. **Hand-placed landmarks:** 4–5 hero models (Citadel gate/flag tower, Trang Tien Bridge, Thien Mu Pagoda tower, market hall) placed at thei
… [truncated 1688 chars — see raw .jsonl]

Base directory for this skill: /home/delus/.claude/plugins/cache/delus-plugins/superpowers/5.0.8/skills/writing-plans

# Writing Plans

## Overview

Write comprehensive implementation plans assuming the engineer has zero context for our codebase and questionable taste. Document everything they need to know: which files to touch for each task, code, testing, docs they might need to check, how to test it. Give them the whole plan as bite-sized tasks. DRY. YAGNI. TDD. Frequent commits.

Assume they are a skilled developer, but know almost nothing about our toolset or problem domain. Assume they don't know good test design very well.

**Announce at start:** "I'm using the writing-plans skill to create the implementation plan."

**Context:** If working in an isolated worktree, it should have been created via the `superpowers:using-git-worktrees` skill at execution time.

**Save plans to:** `docs/superpowers/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<feature-name>.md`
- (User preferences for plan location override this default)

## Scope Check

If the spec covers multiple independent subsystems, it should have been broken into sub-project specs during brainstorming. If it wasn't, suggest breaking this into separate plans — one per subsystem. Each plan should produce working, testable software on its own.

## File Structure

Before defining tasks, map out which files will be created or modified and what each one is responsible for. This is where decomposition decisions get locked in.

- Design units with clear boundaries and well-defined interfaces. Each file should have one clear responsibility.
- You reason best about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. Prefer smaller, focused files over large ones that do too much.
- Files that change together should live together. Split by responsibility, not by technical layer.
- In existing codebases, follow established patterns. If the codebase uses large files, don't unilaterally restructure - but 
… [truncated 4345 chars — see raw .jsonl]

40	async function fetchOverpass(url: string): Promise<Response> {
41	  return fetch(url, {
42	    method: 'POST',
43	    headers: {
44	      'Content-Type': 'application/x-www-form-urlencoded',
45	      // Overpass rejects requests without a proper User-Agent (returns 406).
46	      'User-Agent': 'hue-quest-world-generator/1.0',
47	      Accept: 'application/json',
48	    },
49	    body: 'data=' + encodeURIComponent(QUERY),
50	  });
51	}
52	
53	const sleep = (ms: number) => new Promise((r) => setTimeout(r, ms));
54	
55	async function getOsm(): Promise<{ elements: OsmElement[] }> {
56	  let lastErr = '';
57	  for (const url of ENDPOINTS) {
58	    for (let attempt = 0; attempt < 2; attempt++) {
59	      const res = await fetchOverpass(url);
60	      if (res.ok) return (await res.json()) as { elements: OsmElement[] };
61	      lastErr = `Overpass error ${res.status} at ${url}`;
62	      // 429/504 are transient rate-limit/timeout responses — retry once after 60s.
63	      if ((res.status === 429 || res.status === 504) && attempt === 0) {
64	        console.warn(`${lastErr}; retrying in 60s...`);
65	        await sleep(60_000);
66	        continue;
67	      }
68	      break; // non-transient (or already retried) — try the next endpoint
69	    }
70	    console.warn(`${lastErr}; falling back to next endpoint...`);
71	  }
72	  throw new Error(lastErr || 'Overpass request failed');
73	}

```
function buildBridge(scene: Scene, pos: Vector3) {
  const root = new TransformNode('bridge', scene);
  root.position = pos;
  const steel = tint(scene, '#b8bfc9');
  // Deck crossing the river roughly north-south at this point.
  const deck = MeshBuilder.CreateBox('deck', { width: 8, depth: 130, height: 0.5 }, scene);
  deck.position.y = 1.2;
  deck.material = tint(scene, '#7d7d7d');
  deck.parent = root;
  // 6 arches along the deck.
  for (let i = 0; i < 6; i++) {
    const zOff = -52 + i * 21;
    const path: Vector3[] = [];
    for (let s = 0; s <= 10; s++) {
      const t = s / 10;
      path.push(new Vector3(0, 1.2 + Math.sin(t * Math.PI) * 5, zOff + t * 20));
    }
    [-3.6, 3.6].forEach((x, side) => {
      const tube = MeshBuilder.CreateTube(`arch${i}-${side}`, {
        path: path.map((p) => new Vector3(x, p.y, p.z)),
        radius: 0.35,
      }, scene);
      tube.material = steel;
      tube.parent = root;
    });
  }
}

function buildMarket(scene: Scene, pos: Vector3) {
  const root = new TransformNode('market', scene);
```

Verdict: Dong Ba market (dense buildings, ~21 fps), the mid-bridge over water (~20.5 fps), and the running test (~20 fps) are all below the 30fps software-rendering threshold and worth flagging — these are the spots with the most simultaneous draw calls/overdraw (dense building clusters, water shader, or continuous movement forcing new chunks/culling each frame). Spawn area (40.8fps) and citadel gate (30.1fps) are comfortably fine. Given software rendering typically undersells real GPU performance by several multiples, these numbers alone aren't necessarily a red flag for real hardware, but the relative pattern — dense-geometry areas and water areas being ~2x slower than spawn — suggests those are the areas to profile first if real-device FPS complaints come in (likely draw-call count on buildings, or the water material's shader cost).

No console errors were captured during the run.

Babylon.js + Vite + TypeScript, no physics engine (moveWithCollisions on flat ground, player y locked at 0.9).\n\nKey facts not obvious from code:\n- Dev server must run with `--host 0.0.0.0` — user plays from Windows while code runs in WSL2 (`npx vite --host 0.0.0.0 --port 5173`).\n- `npm run generate` re-fetches OSM via Overpass and rewrites `public/world.json` (committed snapshot). Landmark/NPC/area coords are lat/lon so they survive regeneration.\n- The Perfume River comes from a multipolygon *relation*; generator stitches outer segments into rings and clips to bbox. If water breaks after regen, check `assembleRings` in scripts/generate-world.ts first.\n- Bridge crossing works via measured bank crossings: main.ts computes where the bridge line crosses the river polygon, opens gaps in the invisible bank-wall collision there, and sizes the deck to the real ~440 m span.\n- `window.__scene` debug hook in main.ts is required by `scripts/e2e.mjs` (Playwright smoke test: full 2-quest playthrough + persistence + bank-collision negative test). Run with dev server up: `node scripts/e2e.mjs`.\n- Headless FPS numbers are SwiftShader (software) — 20-40 fps there ≈ fine on real GPU.\n- Spec/plan: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-17-hue-quest-design.md, docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-17-hue-quest.md.\n\nUser preferences observed: approved multi-agent builds (\"spawn agent teams\", sonnet for speed), skipped strict review gates for this project.\n"}`

### 🤖 Assistant  ·  _2026-07-17T08:53:36.733Z_

**Huế Quest is done and verified — playing now at http://localhost:5173** (or http://192.168.0.79:5173 from another device; the server stays up).

## What you got

A single-player 2.5D open-world browser game set in a low-poly Huế built from real OpenStreetMap data: 1,741 buildings, the full street grid, the Citadel with walls and moat, and the Perfume River. You walk in third-person (WASD, Shift to run), cross a properly-sized 440m Trang Tien Bridge, and play two quests across five NPCs (E to talk, Tab for the quest log): deliver Minh's letter to the Citadel guard, and recover Bà Hoa's lantern from the pagoda garden. Progress persists across reloads.

## Verification results

- **E2E playthrough (Sonnet agent):** all 9 assertions passed — fresh load, both quests end-to-end, quest-log states, lantern disappearing, mid-quest reload persistence, zero console errors, and the river correctly blocks swimming while the bridge stays crossable.
- **Performance (Sonnet agent):** 20–40 fps under headless *software* rendering, which maps to comfortable real-GPU framerates; the dense market area is the first place to look if your machine ever dips.
- **Unit tests:** 16 passing (geo math, dialogue runner, quest machine). Production build succeeds.

## How it was built

Spec → plan → three agent waves (foundation / parallel systems / integration), then I did the visual QA loop the agents couldn't: screenshots revealed the river was rendering *under* the ground plane, the river relation needed ring-stitching in the generator, and the bridge was both too short (130m vs the real 440m) and walled off by water collision — all fixed and re-verified. History is 7 clean commits in the new git repo.

Worth knowing: `npm run generate` re-snapshots OSM (the world is a committed file — no runtime API dependency, and the pipeline takes any bounding box if you want a different city later), and `node scripts/e2e.mjs` re-runs the full playthrough test whenever you change something. Natural next 
… [truncated 124 chars — see raw .jsonl]

10	  }
11	
12	  private handle(e: KeyboardEvent, down: boolean) {
13	    switch (e.code) {
14	      case 'KeyW': case 'ArrowUp': this.up = down; break;
15	      case 'KeyS': case 'ArrowDown': this.down = down; break;
16	      case 'KeyA': case 'ArrowLeft': this.left = down; break;
17	      case 'KeyD': case 'ArrowRight': this.right = down; break;
18	      case 'ShiftLeft': case 'ShiftRight': this.run = down; break;
19	      case 'KeyE': if (down && !e.repeat) this.interactPressed = true; break;
20	      case 'Tab': e.preventDefault(); if (down && !e.repeat) this.toggleLogPressed = true; break;
21	      case 'Digit1': case 'Digit2': case 'Digit3':
22	        if (down && !e.repeat) this.choicePressed = Number(e.code.slice(-1)) - 1;
23	        break;
24	    }
25	  }
26	
27	  consumeInteract(): boolean { const v = this.interactPressed; this.interactPressed = false; return v; }
28	  consumeToggleLog(): boolean { const v = this.toggleLogPressed; this.toggleLogPressed = false; return v; }

### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-17T09:37:34.255Z_

📎 _tool result_:
```
36	  /** Returns true if the player moved this frame. */
37	  update(dt: number, input: Input, frozen: boolean): boolean {
38	    let mx = 0;
39	    let mz = 0;
40	    if (!frozen) {
41	      mx = (input.right ? 1 : 0) - (input.left ? 1 : 0);
42	      mz = (input.up ? 1 : 0) - (input.down ? 1 : 0);
43	    }
44	    const len = Math.hypot(mx, mz);
45	    const moving = len > 0;
46	    if (moving) {
47	      mx /= len;
48	      mz /= len;
49	      // camera-relative movement: W walks where the camera looks
50	      const cy = this.camYaw;
51	      const wx = mx * Math.cos(cy) + mz * Math.sin(cy);
52	      const wz = -mx * Math.sin(cy) + mz * Math.cos(cy);
53	      const speed = input.run ? RUN : WALK;
54	      this.mesh.moveWithCollisions(new Vector3(wx * speed * dt, 0, wz * speed * dt));
55	      this.mesh.position.y = CAPSULE_HALF; // flat world: never gain height off collision slopes
56	      this.targetYaw = Math.atan2(wx, wz);
57	    }
58	    // Smooth turn toward movement direction (shortest arc).
59	    let d = this.targetYaw - this.mesh.rotation.y;
60	    d = Math.atan2(Math.sin(d), Math.cos(d));
61	    this.mesh.rotation.y += d * Math.min(1, 12 * dt);
62	
63	    // Camera swings around behind the player's heading while they move.
64	    if (moving) {
65	      let cd = this.mesh.rotation.y - this.camYaw;
66	      cd = Math.atan2(Math.sin(cd), Math.cos(cd));
67	      this.camYaw += cd * Math.min(1, 3.2 * dt);
68	    }
69	    const offset = new Vector3(-Math.sin(this.camYaw) * CAM_DIST, CAM_HEIGHT, -Math.cos(this.camYaw) * CAM_DIST);
70	    const desired = this.mesh.position.add(offset);
71	    const t = 1 - Math.exp(-8 * dt);
72	    this.camera.position = Vector3.Lerp(this.camera.position, desired, t);
73	    this.camera.setTarget(this.mesh.position.add(new Vector3(0, 1.7, 0)));
74	
75	    const state = moving ? (input.run ? 'run' : 'walk') : 'idle';
76	    this.moveState = state;
77	    this.character?.update(dt, state);
78	    return moving;
79	  }
80	}
```

### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-17T10:03:06.845Z_

Another Claude session sent a message:
<teammate-message teammate_id="collect-vr360" color="green" summary="Playwright found real GPS data, rebuilt POIs: 83 total, 71 site-sourced">
Followed up on the VR360 collection using a real browser as requested, and it paid off massively.

The Playwright MCP tool itself couldn't launch in this environment (it requires a system-installed Google Chrome at /opt/google/chrome/chrome, which isn't present, and installing it needs root — sudo asks for a password I don't have). As a substitute that achieves the same result, I used Playwright's own bundled Chromium directly via a Node script (Playwright is already a devDependency here for e2e tests, and its Chromium binary was already cached on this machine).

That let me actually render the JS-heavy tour pages, and it uncovered something the earlier WebFetch pass completely missed: the embedded 360° tour at vr360.com.vn/projects/hue-tourist/ is built with Pano2VR, and it loads its full scene data from an unauthenticated config file, vr360.com.vn/projects/hue-tourist/pano.xml. That file lists 127 individual panorama viewpoints, and every one of them carries a real surveyed GPS latitude/longitude plus a Vietnamese title and English tag — this is VR360's own photogrammetry data, not an approximation.

After deduplicating near-identical viewpoints of the same building (13 separate Trang Tien Bridge photo points collapsed to one entry, etc.), I got 71 distinct, precisely-located landmarks across 7 real complexes: the Imperial Citadel's interior (37 individual halls/gates/temples/watchtowers — Ngọ Môn, Điện Thái Hòa, Cửu Đỉnh, Hiển Lâm Các, Thế Tổ Miếu, Duyệt Thị Đường royal theatre, etc.), Thiên Mụ Pagoda (6 spots), and all three royal tombs — Khải Định, Tự Đức, Minh Mạng — each with 8-10 named sub-locations (gate, stele pavilion, worship hall, burial chamber/lake).

That's **5 quests** total, reflected in the phone HUD counter.
- **Placement corrections:** the surveyed data revealed my flag tower and Ngọ Môn gate were ~300m off — both moved to their true positions, and the guard, his quest area, and district zones followed.

### 🤖 Assistant  ·  _2026-07-17T10:14:16.426Z_

Done and committed (`9ea6927`) — hard-refresh to pick it up.

**What you got:**
- **Click the minimap (or press M)** → a full-city map overlay, scaled to your window: the Perfume River, the Citadel and its moat, every building footprint, the road grid, NPC dots, the gold objective marker, and your position arrow.
- **Click anywhere walkable to teleport** — the camera snaps instantly instead of panning across the city, and the map closes. Clicks on water or buildings are rejected (the map samples its own pixels under your cursor, so you can't strand yourself in the river or inside a building). Esc, M, or clicking the dark backdrop closes it; movement is frozen while the map is up.

Small bonus from the implementation: building footprints are now drawn on the minimap base too, so even the little corner map reads better than before.

Verified headlessly: open via click and via M, a land-click teleport (spawn → citadel, ~1.2km in one click), river-click rejection with the map staying open, Esc close, and all 16 unit tests still green. One note: teleporting into a quest's go-to circle does trigger that step — I left that as-is since it feels like a feature for a demo, but say the word if you want teleport disabled while a trail quest is active.

---

### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-17T10:24:00.445Z_

📎 _tool result_:
```
# DivineVoxelEngine Summary

**What Problem It Solves:**
A TypeScript voxel engine for creating block-based 3D worlds, enabling developers to build Minecraft-like games without building rendering and meshing systems from scratch.

**Renderer:**
Primarily uses Babylon.js via the `@divinevoxel/vlox-babylon` package, with support for both Classic and PBR shaders. Three.js and WebGPU renderers are in development.

**Architecture:**
- **Multi-threaded**: "All meshing and world updates run in parallel"
- **Workers**: Separate worker threads for meshing and world generation
- **Shared Memory**: Optional—can run with or without SharedArrayBuffers
- **Lighting/Physics**: Built-in systems for lighting, flow, power, and collision detection
- **Model System**: JSON-based voxel geometry creation similar to Blockbench

**Maturity & Documentation:**
- 257 GitHub stars, 23 forks; reasonably mature
- Last release: Alpha 1.3.1 (Feb 2023)
- Includes example geometry/model schemas in documentation
- Active Discord community

**Integration (API Surface):**
Games instantiate via `StartRenderer()` with renderer, workers, and voxel data configuration. The "Vlox Model System" lets developers define blocks purely through JSON schemas.

**Design Target:**
Explicitly designed for "Minecraft-like voxel data handling"—specifically block worlds with states, relationships, and custom geometry rather than general low-poly 3D scenes.
```

What changed:
1. Added `DynamicTexture` import and a `createFacadeTexture(scene, baseColorHex, seed)` helper that fills a 256x256 canvas with the bucket's base color, then draws a WINDOWS_PER_TILE x WINDOWS_PER_TILE (4x4) grid of windows with chunky borders (18% cell margin so base wall color shows through as mortar/frame). Windows are dark (#2e3440) with a per-window alpha variation (0.85-1.0), and a WINDOW_LIT_CHANCE (18%) fraction come out warm yellow (#ffd98a) instead. Randomness comes from a seeded mulberry32 PRNG (`seededRandom`), not Math.random, seeded per-bucket as `1000 + i*137` — fully deterministic across builds.
2. Each of the 4 bucket materials now gets its own facade DynamicTexture as `diffuseTexture`, with `uScale = WINDOW_U_SCALE` and `vScale = WINDOW_V_SCALE` (both 0.25, exposed as top-level constants) so windows repeat roughly every 4 local units on the ExtrudePolygon side faces.
3. Roof problem solved via a second mesh, not texture cropping: for every building, alongside the extruded wall mesh I now also build a flat `MeshBuilder.CreatePolygon` cap from the same footprint shape at `y = height + ROOF_Y_OFFSET` (0.05), bucketed the same way (`i % 4`). After the 4 wall-bucket merges, I merge the 4 roof buckets separately and give each a plain (non-textured) material at `darkenHex(BUILDING_COLORS[i], ROOF_DARKEN_FACTOR)` (0.6 darken factor) — no collisions, `freezeWorldMatrix()`. This sits just above the textured top face and fully occludes it.
4. `receiveShadows = true` added to both the building merges and the roof merges (shadow casting is being wired up from main.ts by another agent per your note).

Each boat lerps between the two points at 1.5 m/s with a smoothstep ease on a triangle wave (so it eases in/out at each end and reverses), a sin-based bob (y = 0.15 + sin(t*1.3+phase)*0.08), and yaw computed via atan2 to face travel direction (same convention as the wall-segment rotation math in worldBuilder.ts).

- **Golden-hour Huế**: warm low sun, real cast shadows from buildings/trees/characters, ambient occlusion, subtle bloom and vignette, hazier aerial perspective

- **The city is alive**: five sampan boats drifting the Perfume River, market stalls and lanterns at Đông Ba, lantern strings swaying along Trang Tien Bridge, bird flocks circling, flags on the citadel walls
- **Adaptive quality**: if a machine can't hold 24 fps it sheds SSAO → shadows → post-effects automatically (verified: software rendering steps down to baseline ~21 fps in ~20s; a real GPU keeps everything)

All 16 unit tests and 10/10 E2E assertions still pass, zero console errors.

## Verdict: NO-GO for this hackathon

DVE genuinely works enough to be interesting, but not enough to bet a working game on it.

**What happened:** I installed `@divinevoxel/vlox`/`vlox-babylon` (alpha, 0.0.85/0.0.64), found the npm READMEs are two sentences each with zero programmatic docs, and had to reverse-engineer the API by unpacking the tarballs (805 files of internals) and pulling the one real example (`demos/VloxMinimal`) from GitHub's raw API. From that I built a working prototype: `src/dve-poc/` voxelizes a real 200×200m slice of `public/world.json` around Đông Ba market (33 buildings, 11 roads, 2 water polys) into a custom `WorldGen.generate()` callback, wires up DVE's mandatory 3-worker architecture (World/Mesher/Generator), and renders through DVE's Babylon renderer with an orbit camera. It boots cleanly, no SharedArrayBuffer/COOP-COEP needed, and produces a real screenshot showing correctly-extruded building footprints on grass voxels at 1m resolution.

**Why NO-GO:**
- No usable docs — the only "documentation" is reading library source and demo code, which alone burned most of the time-box for just a small slice, not the full map.
- Public API is unstable deep-file imports (`@divinevoxel/vlox/Tasks/WorldGeneration/WorldGeneration`) with no `exports` map or semver stability — packages publish weekly.
- The prototype under-populates the requested are
… [truncated 1423 chars — see raw .jsonl]

### 🤖 Assistant  ·  _2026-07-17T10:45:24.017Z_

**Engine decision: stay on Babylon — the DVE prototype settled it with evidence.**

The evaluation agent did the work honestly: it actually got DivineVoxelEngine running (installed the alpha packages, reverse-engineered the undocumented API from the package internals, voxelized a real 200×200m slice of our OSM data around Đông Ba market, wired up DVE's 3-worker architecture). The screenshot above is the result. The verdict was **NO-GO** for this project:

- **~11–16 fps for that tiny fragment** vs. 60 fps for our *entire city* today — DVE's chunk meshing fights the low-draw-call merging we already do
- **Zero documentation** — the API had to be learned by reading 800+ files of library source; packages publish weekly with unstable deep-import paths
- The prototype couldn't even fully populate the requested slice (a sector-streaming bug inside the engine that couldn't be root-caused within budget)
- A real migration — collision, characters, quests, content parity — is a **2–3 week rebuild on alpha software**, replacing infrastructure that's polished and verified

Full report with details is committed at `docs/dve-evaluation.md` (+ the prototype screenshot), and the working POC code stays in the agent's worktree if you ever want to revisit it.

Meanwhile the thing you actually wanted — **rendering that feels like being there** — already shipped in the previous commit: golden-hour light and cast shadows, windowed facades, boats on the Perfume River, market lanterns, bird flocks, with automatic quality scaling for weaker machines. Refresh and walk the bridge at "sunset."

If you want to push immersion further on this engine, the highest-value next steps would be: a real sky/sun disc + water reflection shader, ambient audio (river, market chatter, temple bells), and day/night cycle tied to the phone clock. Say the word.
